## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the functional form of a population growth ODE (dP/dt = f(t, P)). The relationship between growth rate and population size is the central question in population dynamics, with classical models ranging from exponential to logistic to more complex density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth model)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Cubic population model: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density dependence)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing over time)
- Logistic with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P * (1 + c2 * P) (seasonal or trending growth rate)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**(c2)) (flexible asymmetric growth)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order density dependence)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting/immigration)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal environmental variation)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolic-catabolic balance model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative quadratic term in P (c0*P + c1*P^2 with c1<0) → density-dependent self-limitation / carrying capacity behavior
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria (e.g., Allee effect creates unstable lower threshold)
- Logarithmic dependence on P (P*log(P)) → Gompertz-type asymmetric growth where decline rate slows near carrying capacity
- Rational function of P (P/(1+cP)) → resource competition with handling time or interference effects
- Additive constant term independent of P → immigration, harvesting, or external population flux
- Sinusoidal time dependence multiplied by growth term → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Fractional power of P (P^c with 0<c<1) → sub-linear scaling typical of metabolic or allometric constraints
- Exponential time factor multiplying growth rate → non-stationary environment with trending resource availability
- Zero growth rate at P=0 (no constant term) → population cannot spontaneously generate without existing individuals
- Sign change in dP/dt as P increases → existence of stable equilibrium (carrying capacity) indicated by root crossing
